The two men quickly bonded, as Sukarno was attracted to Guevara's energy and his relaxed informal approach; moreover they shared revolutionary [leftist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-wing_politics "Left-wing politics") aspirations against Western [imperialism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism "Imperialism").<sup id="cite_ref-Merdeka_143-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Merdeka-143">[143]</a></sup> Guevara next spent 12 days in Japan (15–27 July), participating in negotiations aimed at expanding Cuba's trade relations with that country. During the visit he refused to visit and lay a wreath at Japan's [Tomb of the Unknown Soldier](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier "Tomb of the Unknown Soldier") commemorating soldiers lost during [World War II](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), remarking that the Japanese "imperialists" had "killed millions of Asians".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997431_144-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997431-144">[144]</a></sup> Instead, Guevara stated that he would visit [Hiroshima](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hiroshima "Hiroshima"), where the American military had [detonated](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki") an [atomic bomb](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Little_Boy "Little Boy") 14 years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997431_144-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997431-144">[144]</a></sup> Despite his denunciation of [Imperial Japan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan"), Guevara considered [President Truman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_S._Truman "Harry S. Truman") a "macabre clown" for the bombings,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaibo1999300_145-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaibo1999300-145">[145]</a></sup> and after visiting Hiroshima and its [Peace Memorial Museum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Memorial_Museum "Hiroshima Peace Memorial Museum") he sent back a postcard to Cuba stating, "In order to fight better for peace, one must look at Hiroshima."<sup id="cite_ref-146"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>

Upon Guevara's return to Cuba in September 1959, it became evident that Castro now had more political power. The government had begun land seizures in accordance with the agrarian reform law, but was hedging on compensation offers to landowners, instead offering low-interest "bonds", a step which put the United States on alert. At this point the affected wealthy cattlemen of [Camagüey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camag%C3%BCey "Camagüey") mounted a campaign against the land redistributions and enlisted the newly disaffected rebel leader [Huber Matos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huber_Matos "Huber Matos"), who along with the [anti-communist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communism "Anti-communism") wing of the 26 July Movement, joined them in denouncing "communist encroachment".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997435_147-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997435-147">[147]</a></sup> During this time Dominican dictator [Rafael Trujillo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo "Rafael Trujillo") was offering assistance to the "[Anti-Communist Legion of the Caribbean](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Communist_Legion_of_the_Caribbean "Anti-Communist Legion of the Caribbean")" which was training in the Dominican Republic. This multi-national force, composed mostly of Spaniards and Cubans, but also of Croatians, Germans, Greeks, and right-wing mercenaries, was plotting to topple Castro's new regime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997435_147-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997435-147">[147]</a></sup>

At this stage, Guevara acquired the additional position of Minister of Finance, as well as President of the [National Bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Cuba "Central Bank of Cuba").<sup id="cite_ref-148"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> These appointments, combined with his existing position as Minister of Industries, placed Guevara at the zenith of his power, as the "virtual czar" of the Cuban economy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198955_149-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198955-149">[149]</a></sup> As a consequence of his position at the head of the central bank, it became Guevara's duty to sign the Cuban currency, which per custom bore his signature. Instead of using his full name, he signed the bills solely "_Che_".<sup id="cite_ref-Crompton2009_150-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Crompton2009-150">[150]</a></sup> It was through this symbolic act, which horrified many in the Cuban financial sector, that Guevara signaled his distaste for money and the class distinctions it brought about.<sup id="cite_ref-Crompton2009_150-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Crompton2009-150">[150]</a></sup> Guevara's long time friend Ricardo Rojo later remarked that "the day he signed _Che_ on the bills, (he) literally knocked the props from under the widespread belief that money was sacred."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198960_151-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198960-151">[151]</a></sup>

International threats were heightened when, on 4 March 1960, two massive explosions ripped through the French freighter _[La Coubre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Coubre_explosion "La Coubre explosion")_, which was carrying [Belgian munitions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/FN_FAL "FN FAL") from the port of [Antwerp](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antwerp "Antwerp"), and was docked in [Havana Harbor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Havana_Harbor "Havana Harbor"). The blasts killed at least 76 people and injured several hundred, with Guevara personally providing first aid to some of the victims. Fidel Castro immediately accused the CIA of "an act of terrorism" and held a state funeral the following day for the victims of the blast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECasey200925_152-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTECasey200925-152">[152]</a></sup> At the memorial service [Alberto Korda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alberto_Korda "Alberto Korda") took the famous photograph of Guevara, now known as _[Guerrillero Heroico](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara_(photo) "Che Guevara (photo)")_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECasey200925–50_153-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTECasey200925%E2%80%9350-153">[153]</a></sup>

Perceived threats prompted Castro to eliminate more "[counter-revolutionaries](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counter-revolutionary "Counter-revolutionary")" and to utilize Guevara to drastically increase the speed of [land reform](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_reform "Land reform"). To implement this plan, a new government agency, the [National Institute of Agrarian Reform](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Reforma_Agraria "Instituto Nacional de Reforma Agraria") (INRA), was established by the Cuban government to administer the new agrarian reform law. INRA quickly became the most important governing body in the nation, with Guevara serving as its head in his capacity as minister of industries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198958_137-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198958-137">[137]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (June 2019)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> Under Guevara's command, INRA established its own 100,000-person militia, used first to help the government seize control of the expropriated land and supervise its distribution, and later to set up cooperative farms. The land confiscated included 480,000 acres (190,000 ha) owned by United States corporations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198958_137-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198958-137">[137]</a></sup> Months later, in retaliation, US President [Dwight D. Eisenhower](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower "Dwight D. Eisenhower") sharply reduced United States imports of [Cuban sugar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_sugar_economy "Cuban sugar economy") (Cuba's main cash crop), which led Guevara on 10 July 1960 to address over 100,000 workers in front of the [Presidential Palace](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Museum_of_the_Revolution_(Cuba) "Museum of the Revolution (Cuba)") at a rally to denounce the "economic aggression" of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198955_149-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198955-149">[149]</a></sup> [_Time Magazine_](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_(magazine) "Time (magazine)") reporters who met with Guevara around this time described him as "guid(ing) Cuba with icy calculation, vast competence, high intelligence, and a perceptive sense of humor."<sup id="cite_ref-Castrosbrain1960_8-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Castrosbrain1960-8">[8]</a></sup>

> Guevara was like a father to me ... he educated me. He taught me to think. He taught me the most beautiful thing which is to be human.

—Urbano <small>(a.k.a. Leonardo Tamayo)</small>,  
fought with Guevara in Cuba and Bolivia<sup id="cite_ref-154"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>

Along with land reform, Guevara stressed the need for national improvement in [literacy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literacy "Literacy"). Before 1959 the official literacy rate for Cuba was between 60 and 76%, with educational access in rural areas and a lack of instructors the main determining factors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198961_155-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198961-155">[155]</a></sup> As a result, the Cuban government at Guevara's behest dubbed 1961 the "year of education" and mobilized over 100,000 volunteers into "literacy brigades", who were then sent out into the countryside to construct schools, train new educators, and teach the predominantly illiterate _guajiros_ (peasants) to read and write.<sup id="cite_ref-LiteracyC_88-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-LiteracyC-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198961_155-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198961-155">[155]</a></sup> Unlike many of Guevara's later economic initiatives, this campaign was "a remarkable success". By the completion of the [Cuban literacy campaign](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_literacy_campaign "Cuban literacy campaign"), 707,212 adults had been taught to read and write, raising the national literacy rate to 96%.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198961_155-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198961-155">[155]</a></sup>

Accompanying literacy, Guevara was also concerned with establishing universal access to higher education. To accomplish this the new regime introduced [affirmative action](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affirmative_action "Affirmative action") to the universities. While announcing this new commitment, Guevara told the gathered faculty and students at the [University of Las Villas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_%22Marta_Abreu%22_of_Las_Villas "University "Marta Abreu" of Las Villas") that the days when education was "a privilege of the white middle class" had ended. "The University" he said, "must paint itself black, mulatto, worker, and peasant." If it did not, he warned, the people were going to break down its doors "and paint the University the colors they like."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997449_156-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997449-156">[156]</a></sup>

### Economic reforms and the "New Man"

In September 1960, when Guevara was asked about Cuba's ideology at the First Latin American Congress, he replied, "If I were asked whether our revolution is Communist, I would define it as [Marxist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism "Marxism"). Our revolution has discovered by its methods the paths that Marx pointed out."<sup id="cite_ref-157"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Consequently, when enacting and advocating Cuban policy, Guevara cited the political philosopher [Karl Marx](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx "Karl Marx") as his ideological inspiration. In defending his political stance, Guevara confidently remarked, "There are truths so evident, so much a part of people's knowledge, that it is now useless to discuss them. One ought to be Marxist with the same naturalness with which one is '[Newtonian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newtonian_dynamics "Newtonian dynamics")' in [physics](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physics "Physics"), or '[Pasteurian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Pasteur "Louis Pasteur")' in [biology](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology "Biology")."<sup id="cite_ref-Notes1960_158-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Notes1960-158">[158]</a></sup> According to Guevara, the "practical revolutionaries" of the Cuban Revolution had the goal of "simply fulfill(ing) laws foreseen by Marx, the scientist."<sup id="cite_ref-Notes1960_158-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Notes1960-158">[158]</a></sup> Using Marx's predictions and system of [dialectical materialism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dialectical_materialism "Dialectical materialism"), Guevara professed that "The laws of Marxism are present in the events of the Cuban Revolution, independently of what its leaders profess or fully know of those laws from a theoretical point of view."<sup id="cite_ref-Notes1960_158-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Notes1960-158">[158]</a></sup>

> The merit of Marx is that he suddenly produces a qualitative change in the history of social thought. He interprets history, understands its dynamic, predicts the future, but in addition to predicting it (which would satisfy his scientific obligation), he expresses a revolutionary concept: the world must not only be interpreted, it must be transformed. Man ceases to be the slave and tool of his environment and converts himself into the architect of his own destiny.
> 
> — Che Guevara, _Notes for the Study of the Ideology of the Cuban_, October 1960 <sup id="cite_ref-Notes1960_158-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Notes1960-158">[158]</a></sup>

> Man truly achieves his full human condition when he produces without being compelled by the physical necessity of selling himself as a commodity.
> 
> — Che Guevara, _Man and Socialism in Cuba_<sup id="cite_ref-159"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Beauvoir_Sartre_-_Che_Guevara_-1960_-_Cuba.jpg)

Guevara meeting with French [existentialist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existentialism "Existentialism") philosophers [Jean-Paul Sartre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Paul_Sartre "Jean-Paul Sartre") and [Simone de Beauvoir](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simone_de_Beauvoir "Simone de Beauvoir") at his office in Havana, March 1960. Sartre later wrote that Che was _"the most complete human being of our time"_. In addition to Spanish, Guevara was fluent in French.<sup id="cite_ref-160"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup>

In an effort to eliminate [social inequalities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_inequality "Social inequality"), Guevara and Cuba's new leadership had moved to swiftly transform the political and economic base of the country through [nationalizing](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalization "Nationalization") factories, banks, and businesses, while attempting to ensure affordable housing, healthcare, and employment for all Cubans.<sup id="cite_ref-Hansing4142_161-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Hansing4142-161">[161]</a></sup> In order for a genuine transformation of consciousness to take root, it was believed that such structural changes had to be accompanied by a conversion in people's [social relations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_relation "Social relation") and [values](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_(ethics_and_social_sciences)#Value_system "Value (ethics and social sciences)"). Believing that the attitudes in Cuba towards [race](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racism_in_Cuba "Racism in Cuba"), [women](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Cuba "Women in Cuba"), [individualism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Individualism "Individualism"), and [manual labor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manual_labour "Manual labour") were the product of the island's outdated past, all individuals were urged to view each other as equals and take on the values of what Guevara termed _"el Hombre Nuevo"_ (the New Man).<sup id="cite_ref-Hansing4142_161-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Hansing4142-161">[161]</a></sup> Guevara hoped his "new man" to be ultimately "selfless and cooperative, obedient and hard working, [gender-blind](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender-blind "Gender-blind"), incorruptible, [non-materialistic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-consumerism "Anti-consumerism"), and [anti-imperialist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-imperialism "Anti-imperialism")".<sup id="cite_ref-Hansing4142_161-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Hansing4142-161">[161]</a></sup> To accomplish this, Guevara emphasized the tenets of [Marxism–Leninism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism "Marxism–Leninism"), and wanted to use the state to emphasize qualities such as [egalitarianism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egalitarianism "Egalitarianism") and [self-sacrifice](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-denial "Self-denial"), at the same time as "unity, equality, and freedom" became the new maxims.<sup id="cite_ref-Hansing4142_161-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Hansing4142-161">[161]</a></sup> Guevara's first desired economic goal of the new man, which coincided with his aversion for [wealth condensation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distribution_of_wealth#Wealth_concentration "Distribution of wealth") and [economic inequality](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_inequality "Economic inequality"), was to see a nationwide elimination of material incentives in favor of [moral](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morality "Morality") ones. He negatively viewed capitalism as a "contest among wolves" where "one can only win at the cost of others" and thus desired to see the creation of a "new man and woman".<sup id="cite_ref-SocialismAndMan_162-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-SocialismAndMan-162">[162]</a></sup> Guevara continually stressed that a socialist economy in itself is not "worth the effort, sacrifice, and risks of war and destruction" if it ends up encouraging "greed and individual ambition at the expense of [collective spirit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_organization#Collectivism_and_individualism "Social organization")".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198962_163-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198962-163">[163]</a></sup> A primary goal of Guevara's thus became to reform "individual consciousness" and values to produce better workers and citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198962_163-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198962-163">[163]</a></sup> In his view, Cuba's "new man" would be able to overcome the "[egotism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egotism "Egotism")" and "[selfishness](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selfishness "Selfishness")" that he loathed and discerned was uniquely characteristic of individuals in capitalist societies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198962_163-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198962-163">[163]</a></sup> To promote this concept of a "new man", the government also created a series of party-dominated institutions and mechanisms on all levels of society, which included organizations such as [labor groups](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_movement "Labour movement"), [youth leagues](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Communist_League_(Cuba) "Young Communist League (Cuba)"), [women's groups](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federation_of_Cuban_Women "Federation of Cuban Women"), [community centers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_centre "Community centre"), and [houses of culture](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palace_of_Culture "Palace of Culture") to promote state-sponsored art, music, and literature. In congruence with this, all educational, mass media, and artistic community based facilities were nationalized and utilized to instill the government's official [socialist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_mode_of_production "Socialist mode of production") ideology.<sup id="cite_ref-Hansing4142_161-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Hansing4142-161">[161]</a></sup> In describing this new method of "development", Guevara stated:

> There is a great difference between free-enterprise development and revolutionary development. In one of them, wealth is concentrated in the hands of a fortunate few, the friends of the government, the best wheeler-dealers. In the other, wealth is the people's patrimony.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198959_164-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198959-164">[164]</a></sup>

A further integral part of fostering a sense of "unity between the individual and the mass", Guevara believed, was volunteer work and will. To display this, Guevara "led by example", working "endlessly at his ministry job, in construction, and even cutting sugar cane" on his day off.<sup id="cite_ref-165"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> He was known for working 36 hours at a stretch, calling meetings after midnight, and eating on the run.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198962_163-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198962-163">[163]</a></sup> Such behavior was emblematic of Guevara's new program of moral incentives, where each worker was now required to meet a quota and produce a certain quantity of goods. As a replacement for the pay increases abolished by Guevara, workers who exceeded their quota now only received a certificate of commendation, while workers who failed to meet their quotas were given a pay cut.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198962_163-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198962-163">[163]</a></sup> Guevara unapologetically defended his personal philosophy towards motivation and work, stating:

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CheFishing.jpg)

Guevara fishing off the coast of Havana, on 15 May 1960. Along with Castro, Guevara competed with expatriate author [Ernest Hemingway](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway "Ernest Hemingway") at what was known as the "[Hemingway Fishing Contest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway_International_Billfishing_Tournament "Ernest Hemingway International Billfishing Tournament")".

> This is not a matter of how many pounds of meat one might be able to eat, or how many times a year someone can go to the beach, or how many ornaments from abroad one might be able to buy with his current salary. What really matters is that the individual feels more complete, with much more internal richness and much more responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198975_166-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198975-166">[166]</a></sup>

In the face of a loss of commercial connections with Western states, Guevara tried to replace them with closer commercial relationships with [Eastern Bloc](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") states, visiting a number of Marxist states and signing trade agreements with them. At the end of 1960 he visited [Czechoslovakia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic "Czechoslovak Socialist Republic"), the [Soviet Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union"), [North Korea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea"), [Hungary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic "Hungarian People's Republic"), and [East Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") and signed, for instance, a trade agreement in [East Berlin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Berlin "East Berlin") on 17 December 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-167"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Such agreements helped Cuba's economy to a certain degree but also had the disadvantage of a growing economic dependency on the Eastern Bloc. It was also in East Germany where Guevara met [Tamara Bunke](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamara_Bunke "Tamara Bunke") (later known as "Tania"), who was assigned as his interpreter, and who joined him years later, and was killed with him in Bolivia.

According to Douglas Kellner, his programs were unsuccessful,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198963_168-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198963-168">[168]</a></sup> and accompanied a rapid drop in productivity and a rapid rise in absenteeism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198974_169-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198974-169">[169]</a></sup> In a meeting with French economist [René Dumont](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Dumont "René Dumont"), Guevara blamed the inadequacy of the agrarian reform law enacted by the Cuban government in 1959, which turned large plantations into farm [cooperatives](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooperative "Cooperative") or split up land amongst peasants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaibo1999269_170-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaibo1999269-170">[170]</a></sup> In Guevara's opinion, this situation continued to promote a "heightened sense of individual ownership" in which workers could not see the positive social benefits of their labor, leading them to instead seek individual material gain as before.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaibo1999306_171-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaibo1999306-171">[171]</a></sup> Decades later, Che's former deputy Ernesto Betancourt, subsequently the director of the US government-funded [Radio Martí](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_y_Televisi%C3%B3n_Mart%C3%AD "Radio y Televisión Martí") and an early ally turned Castro-critic, accused Guevara of being "ignorant of the most elementary economic principles."<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_172-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-ReferenceB-172">[172]</a></sup>

### Bay of Pigs Invasion and Missile Crisis

On 17 April 1961, 1,400 US-trained Cuban exiles invaded Cuba during the [Bay of Pigs Invasion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion "Bay of Pigs Invasion"). Guevara did not play a key role in the fighting, as one day before the invasion a warship carrying Marines faked an invasion off the West Coast of [Pinar del Río](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinar_del_R%C3%ADo "Pinar del Río") and drew forces commanded by Guevara to that region. However, historians give him a share of credit for the victory as he was director of instruction for Cuba's armed forces at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198969–70_10-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198969%E2%80%9370-10">[10]</a></sup> Author [Tad Szulc](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tad_Szulc "Tad Szulc") in his explanation of the Cuban victory, assigns Guevara partial credit, stating: "The revolutionaries won because Che Guevara, as the head of the Instruction Department of the Revolutionary Armed Forces in charge of the militia training program, had done so well in preparing 200,000 men and women for war."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198969–70_10-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198969%E2%80%9370-10">[10]</a></sup> It was also during this deployment that he suffered a bullet grazing to the cheek when his pistol fell out of its holster and accidentally discharged.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997507_173-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997507-173">[173]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg)

Guevara (left) and [Fidel Castro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro "Fidel Castro"), photographed by Alberto Korda in 1961

In August 1961, during an economic conference of the [Organization of American States](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_of_American_States "Organization of American States") in [Punta del Este](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punta_del_Este "Punta del Este"), Uruguay, Che Guevara sent a note of "gratitude" to United States President [John F. Kennedy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy "John F. Kennedy") through [Richard N. Goodwin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_N._Goodwin "Richard N. Goodwin"), Deputy Assistant Secretary of State for Inter-American Affairs. It read "Thanks for Playa Girón (Bay of Pigs). Before the invasion, the revolution was shaky. Now it's stronger than ever."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997509_174-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997509-174">[174]</a></sup> In response to United States Treasury Secretary [Douglas Dillon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/C._Douglas_Dillon "C. Douglas Dillon") presenting the [Alliance for Progress](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alliance_for_Progress "Alliance for Progress") for ratification by the meeting, Guevara antagonistically attacked the United States' claim of being a "democracy", stating that such a system was not compatible with "financial [oligarchy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oligarchy "Oligarchy"), [discrimination against blacks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States "Racial segregation in the United States"), and outrages by the [Ku Klux Klan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan "Ku Klux Klan")".<sup id="cite_ref-PuntaDelEsteChe_175-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-PuntaDelEsteChe-175">[175]</a></sup> Guevara continued, speaking out against the "persecution" that in his view "drove scientists like [Oppenheimer](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Robert_Oppenheimer "J. Robert Oppenheimer") from their posts, deprived the world for years of the marvelous voice of [Paul Robeson](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Robeson "Paul Robeson"), and sent the [Rosenbergs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_and_Ethel_Rosenberg "Julius and Ethel Rosenberg") to their deaths against the protests of a shocked world."<sup id="cite_ref-PuntaDelEsteChe_175-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-PuntaDelEsteChe-175">[175]</a></sup> Guevara ended his remarks by insinuating that the United States was not interested in real reforms, sardonically quipping that "U.S. experts never talk about agrarian reform; they prefer a safe subject, like a better water supply. In short, they seem to prepare the revolution of the toilets."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198978_176-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198978-176">[176]</a></sup> Nevertheless, Goodwin stated in his memo to President Kennedy following the meeting that Guevara viewed him as someone of the "newer generation"<sup id="cite_ref-goodwinche_177-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-goodwinche-177">[177]</a></sup> and that Guevara, whom Goodwin alleged sent a message to him the day after the meeting through one of the meeting's Argentine participants whom he described as "Darretta,"<sup id="cite_ref-goodwinche_177-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-goodwinche-177">[177]</a></sup> also viewed the conversation which the two had as "quite profitable."<sup id="cite_ref-goodwinche_177-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-goodwinche-177">[177]</a></sup>

Guevara, who was practically the architect of the [Cuban–Soviet relationship](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93Soviet_Union_relations "Cuba–Soviet Union relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997492_178-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997492-178">[178]</a></sup> played a key role in bringing to Cuba the Soviet [nuclear-armed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon") [ballistic missiles](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballistic_missile "Ballistic missile") that precipitated the [Cuban Missile Crisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis "Cuban Missile Crisis") in October 1962 and brought the world to the brink of [nuclear war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_warfare "Nuclear warfare").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997530_179-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997530-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> After the Soviets proposed planting nuclear missiles in Cuba it was Che Guevara himself who traveled to the Soviet Union on 30 August 1962, to sign off on the final agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-181"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> Guevara argued with Khruschev that the missile deal should be made public but Khruschev insisted on secrecy, and swore the Soviet Union's support if the Americans discovered the missiles. By the time Guevara arrived in Cuba the United States had already discovered the Soviet troops in Cuba via U-2 spy planes.<sup id="cite_ref-182"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup>

A few weeks after the crisis, during an interview with the British communist newspaper the _[Daily Worker](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morning_Star_(British_newspaper) "Morning Star (British newspaper)")_, Guevara was still fuming over the perceived Soviet betrayal and told correspondent Sam Russell that, if the missiles had been under Cuban control, they would have fired them off.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997545_183-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997545-183">[183]</a></sup> While expounding on the incident later, Guevara reiterated that the cause of socialist liberation against global "imperialist aggression" would ultimately have been worth the possibility of "millions of atomic war victims".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuevaraDeutschmann1997304_184-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuevaraDeutschmann1997304-184">[184]</a></sup> The missile crisis further convinced Guevara that the world's two superpowers (the United States and the Soviet Union) used Cuba as a pawn in their own global strategies. Afterward, he denounced the Soviets almost as frequently as he denounced the Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198973_185-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198973-185">[185]</a></sup>

### Great Debate

The era in Cuban history retroactively named the "Great Debate" by historians was defined by public debate about the future of Cuban economic policy that took place from 1962 to 1965. The debate began after Cuba fell into an economic crisis in 1962 after years of internal economic complications, [United States sanctions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba "United States embargo against Cuba"), and [the flight of professionals from Cuba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_exile "Golden exile"). In 1962 [Fidel Castro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro "Fidel Castro") invited Marxist economists around the world to debate two main propositions. One proposition proposed by Che Guevara was that Cuba could bypass any capitalist then "socialist" transition period and immediately become an industrialized "communist" society if "subjective conditions" like public consciousness and vanguard action are perfected. The other proposition held by the [Popular Socialist Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Socialist_Party_(Cuba) "Popular Socialist Party (Cuba)") was that Cuba required a transitionary period as a [mixed economy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed_economy "Mixed economy") in which Cuba's sugar economy was maximized for profit before a "communist" society could be established.<sup id="cite_ref-def_186-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-def-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>

Guevara elaborated in this period that moral incentives should exist as the main motivator to increase workers' production. All profits created by enterprises were to be given to the state budget, and the state budget would cover losses. Institutions that developed socialist consciousness were regarded as the most important element in maintaining a path to socialism rather than materially incentivized increases in production. Implementation of the profit-motive was regarded as a path towards capitalism and as one of the flaws of the [Eastern bloc](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_bloc "Eastern bloc") economies.<sup id="cite_ref-189"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> The economy would also rely on mass mobilizations and centralized planning as a method for developing the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-soviets_190-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-soviets-190">[190]</a></sup> The main ideal that compromised the consciousness that would develop socialism was the praise of the "new man", a citizen that was only motivated by human solidarity and self-sacrifice.<sup id="cite_ref-191"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup>

In 1966 the Cuban economy was reorganized on moral lines. Cuban propaganda stressed voluntarism and ideological motivations to increase productions. Material incentives were not given to workers who were more productive than others.<sup id="cite_ref-Leadership_192-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Leadership-192">[192]</a></sup> Cuban intellectuals were expected to participate actively in creating a positive national ethos and ignore any desire to create "art for art's sake".<sup id="cite_ref-fifties_193-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-fifties-193">[193]</a></sup> In 1968 all non-agricultural private businesses were nationalized, central planning was done more on an ad-hoc basis and the entire Cuban economy was directed at producing a 10 million ton sugar harvest. These developments were generally inspired by the resolutions brought about by the Great Debate years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-194"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> The focus on sugar would eventually render all other facets of the Cuban economy underdeveloped and would be the ultimate legacy of the offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-Leadership_192-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Leadership-192">[192]</a></sup>

## International diplomacy

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CheGuevaraCountries.jpg)

Countries Che Guevara visited (red) and those in which he participated in armed revolution (green)

### United Nations delegation

In December 1964, Che Guevara had emerged as a "revolutionary statesman of world stature" and thus traveled to New York City as head of the Cuban delegation to speak at the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198960_151-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198960-151">[151]</a></sup> On 11 December 1964, during Guevara's hour-long, impassioned address at the UN, he criticized the United Nations' inability to confront the "brutal policy of [apartheid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apartheid "Apartheid")" in South Africa, asking "Can the United Nations do nothing to stop this?".<sup id="cite_ref-GuevaraUnitedNations_195-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-GuevaraUnitedNations-195">[195]</a></sup> Guevara then denounced the [United States policy towards their black population](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Crow_laws "Jim Crow laws"), stating:

> Those who kill their own children and discriminate daily against them because of the color of their skin; those who let the murderers of blacks remain free, protecting them, and furthermore punishing the black population because they demand their legitimate rights as free men—how can those who do this consider themselves guardians of freedom?<sup id="cite_ref-GuevaraUnitedNations_195-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-GuevaraUnitedNations-195">[195]</a></sup>

An indignant Guevara ended his speech by reciting the _Second Declaration of Havana_, decreeing Latin America a "family of 200 million brothers who suffer the same miseries".<sup id="cite_ref-GuevaraUnitedNations_195-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-GuevaraUnitedNations-195">[195]</a></sup> This "epic", Guevara declared, would be written by the "hungry Indian masses, peasants without land, exploited workers, and progressive masses". To Guevara the conflict was a struggle of masses and ideas, which would be carried forth by those "mistreated and scorned by [imperialism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism "Imperialism")" who were previously considered "a weak and submissive flock". With this "flock", Guevara now asserted, "Yankee monopoly capitalism" now terrifyingly saw their "gravediggers".<sup id="cite_ref-GuevaraUnitedNations_195-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-GuevaraUnitedNations-195">[195]</a></sup> It would be during this "hour of vindication", Guevara pronounced, that the "anonymous mass" would begin to write its own history "with its own blood" and reclaim those "rights that were laughed at by one and all for 500 years". Guevara closed his remarks to the General Assembly by hypothesizing that this "wave of anger" would "sweep the lands of Latin America" and that the labor masses who "turn the wheel of history" were now, for the first time, "awakening from the long, brutalizing sleep to which they had been subjected".<sup id="cite_ref-GuevaraUnitedNations_195-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-GuevaraUnitedNations-195">[195]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Chenasser.jpg)

Meeting Egyptian President [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser") in Cairo, 1964

Guevara later learned there had been two failed attempts on his life by [Cuban exiles](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_exile "Cuban exile") during his stop at the UN complex.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTDec1964_196-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-NYTDec1964-196">[196]</a></sup> The first from Molly Gonzales, who tried to break through barricades upon his arrival with a seven-inch hunting knife, and the second by Guillermo Novo, who fired a timer-initiated bazooka from a boat in the [East River](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_River "East River") at the [United Nations Headquarters](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations "Headquarters of the United Nations") during his address, but missed and was off target. Afterwards Guevara commented on both incidents, stating that "it is better to be killed by a woman with a knife than by a man with a gun", while adding with a languid wave of his cigar that the explosion had "given the whole thing more flavor".<sup id="cite_ref-NYTDec1964_196-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-NYTDec1964-196">[196]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CheinMoscow.jpg)

Walking through [Red Square](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Square "Red Square") in Moscow, November 1964

While in New York, Guevara appeared on the [CBS](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/CBS "CBS") Sunday news program _[Face the Nation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Face_the_Nation "Face the Nation"),_<sup id="cite_ref-197"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> and met with a wide range of people, from United States Senator [Eugene McCarthy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_McCarthy "Eugene McCarthy")<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart2004271_198-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart2004271-198">[198]</a></sup> to associates of [Malcolm X](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malcolm_X "Malcolm X"). The latter expressed his admiration, declaring Guevara "one of the most revolutionary men in this country right now" while reading a statement from him to a crowd at the [Audubon Ballroom](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Audubon_Ballroom "Audubon Ballroom").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997618_199-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997618-199">[199]</a></sup>

### World travel

On 17 December, Guevara left New York for Paris, France, and from there embarked on a three-month world tour that included visits to the People's Republic of China, North Korea, the [United Arab Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Republic "United Arab Republic"), Algeria, Ghana, Guinea, Mali, [Dahomey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Dahomey "Republic of Dahomey"), Congo-Brazzaville, and Tanzania, with stops in Ireland and [Prague](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague "Prague"). While in Ireland, Guevara embraced his own Irish heritage, celebrating [Saint Patrick's Day](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Day "Saint Patrick's Day") in [Limerick](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limerick "Limerick").<sup id="cite_ref-200"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> He wrote to his father on this visit, humorously stating "I am in this green Ireland of your ancestors. When they found out, the television \[station\] came to ask me about the Lynch genealogy, but in case they were horse thieves or something like that, I didn't say much."<sup id="cite_ref-201"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> In 1969 Guevara's father was quoted on his sons Irish lineage: "The first thing to note is that in my son’s veins flowed the blood of the Irish rebels..."<sup id="cite_ref-202"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>

During Guevara's time in Algeria he was interviewed by Spanish poet [Juan Goytisolo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Goytisolo "Juan Goytisolo") inside the Cuban embassy. During the interview Guevara noticed a book by openly gay Cuban writer [Virgilio Piñera](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgilio_Pi%C3%B1era "Virgilio Piñera") that was sitting on the table next to him. When he noticed it he threw the book against the wall and yelled "how dare you have in our embassy a book by this foul faggot?".<sup id="cite_ref-203"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Entiendes_205-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Entiendes-205">[205]</a></sup> This moment has been marked as a turn in Goytisolo's personal identity as it influenced him to slowly come out of the closet as gay and begin to sympathize with the LGBT citizens of Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-206"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> This moment has also been marked for its significance in the Cuban government's slow and ultimately final ousting of [Virgilio Piñera](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgilio_Pi%C3%B1era "Virgilio Piñera") from official literary discourse in Cuba. Piñera had originally been regarded as an important dramatist of the Cuban Revolution but had later become slowly condemned and [finally arrested](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Night_of_the_Three_Ps "Night of the Three Ps").<sup id="cite_ref-Entiendes_205-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Entiendes-205">[205]</a></sup>

During this voyage, he wrote a letter to Carlos Quijano, editor of a Uruguayan weekly, which was later retitled _Socialism and Man in Cuba_.<sup id="cite_ref-SocialismAndMan_162-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-SocialismAndMan-162">[162]</a></sup> Outlined in the treatise was Guevara's summons for the creation of a new consciousness, a new status of work, and a new role of the individual. He also laid out the reasoning behind his [anti-capitalist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-capitalism "Anti-capitalism") sentiments, stating:

> The laws of capitalism, blind and invisible to the majority, act upon the individual without his thinking about it. He sees only the vastness of a seemingly infinite horizon before him. That is how it is painted by capitalist propagandists, who purport to draw a lesson from the example of [Rockefeller](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller "John D. Rockefeller")—whether or not it is true—about the possibilities of success. The amount of poverty and suffering required for the emergence of [a Rockefeller](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rockefeller_family "Rockefeller family"), and the amount of depravity that the accumulation of a fortune of such magnitude entails, are left out of the picture, and it is not always possible to make the people in general see this.<sup id="cite_ref-SocialismAndMan_162-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-SocialismAndMan-162">[162]</a></sup>

Guevara ended the essay by declaring that "the true revolutionary is guided by a great feeling of love" and beckoning on all revolutionaries to "strive every day so that this love of living humanity will be transformed into acts that serve as examples", thus becoming "a moving force".<sup id="cite_ref-SocialismAndMan_162-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-SocialismAndMan-162">[162]</a></sup> The genesis for Guevara's assertions relied on the fact that he believed the example of the Cuban Revolution was "something spiritual that would transcend all borders".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson199737–38_38-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson199737%E2%80%9338-38">[38]</a></sup>

### Visit to Algeria and political turn

In [Algiers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers "Algiers"), Algeria, on 24 February 1965, Guevara made what turned out to be his last public appearance on the international stage when he delivered a speech at an economic seminar on Afro-Asian solidarity.<sup id="cite_ref-207"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> He specified the moral duty of the socialist countries, accusing them of tacit complicity with the exploiting Western countries. He proceeded to outline a number of measures which he said the communist-bloc countries must implement in order to accomplish the defeat of [imperialism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism "Imperialism").<sup id="cite_ref-209"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Having criticized the Soviet Union (the primary financial backer of Cuba) in such a public manner, he returned to Cuba on 14 March to a solemn reception by Fidel and Raúl Castro, Osvaldo Dorticós, and Carlos Rafael Rodríguez at the Havana airport.

As revealed in his last public speech in Algiers, Guevara had come to view the [Northern Hemisphere](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere "Northern Hemisphere"), led by the US in the West and the Soviet Union in the East, as the exploiter of the [Southern Hemisphere](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere "Southern Hemisphere"). He strongly supported communist [North Vietnam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Vietnam "North Vietnam") in the [Vietnam War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_War "Vietnam War"), and urged the peoples of other developing countries to take up arms and create "many Vietnams".<sup id="cite_ref-MessTricont1967_210-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-MessTricont1967-210">[210]</a></sup> Che's denunciations of the Soviets made him popular among intellectuals and artists of the Western European left who had lost faith in the Soviet Union, while his condemnation of imperialism and call to revolution inspired young radical students in the United States, who were impatient for societal change.<sup id="cite_ref-Michiko_211-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Michiko-211">[211]</a></sup>

In Guevara's private writings from this time (since released), he displays his growing criticism of the Soviet political economy, believing that the Soviets had "forgotten [Marx](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx "Karl Marx")".<sup id="cite_ref-Yaffe2006_212-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Yaffe2006-212">[212]</a></sup> This led Guevara to denounce a range of Soviet practices including what he saw as their attempt to "air-brush the inherent violence of [class struggle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_conflict "Class conflict") integral to [the transition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communization "Communization") from capitalism to socialism", their "dangerous" policy of [peaceful co-existence](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peaceful_co-existence "Peaceful co-existence") with the United States, their failure to push for a "change in consciousness" towards the idea of work, and their attempt to "[liberalize](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_liberalization "Economic liberalization")" the socialist economy. Guevara wanted the complete elimination of [money](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Money "Money"), [interest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interest "Interest"), [commodity production](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalist_mode_of_production_(Marxist_theory) "Capitalist mode of production (Marxist theory)"), the [market economy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_economy "Market economy"), and "[mercantile relationships](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercantilism "Mercantilism")": all conditions that the Soviets argued would only disappear when [world communism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_communism "World communism") was achieved.<sup id="cite_ref-Yaffe2006_212-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Yaffe2006-212">[212]</a></sup> Disagreeing with this incrementalist approach, Guevara criticized the _Soviet Manual of Political Economy_, correctly predicting that if the Soviet Union did not abolish the [law of value](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_value "Law of value") (as Guevara desired), it would eventually return to capitalism.<sup id="cite_ref-Yaffe2006_212-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-Yaffe2006-212">[212]</a></sup>

Two weeks after his Algiers speech and his return to Cuba, Guevara dropped out of public life and then vanished altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-213"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> His whereabouts were a great mystery in Cuba, as he was generally regarded as second in power to Castro himself. His disappearance was variously attributed to the failure of the Cuban industrialization scheme he had advocated while minister of industries, to pressure exerted on Castro by Soviet officials who disapproved of Guevara's pro-[Chinese communist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party") stance on the [Sino-Soviet split](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split "Sino-Soviet split"), and to serious differences between Guevara and the pragmatic Castro regarding Cuba's economic development and ideological line.<sup id="cite_ref-214"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> Pressed by international speculation regarding Guevara's fate, Castro stated on 16 June 1965, that the people would be informed when Guevara himself wished to let them know. Still, rumors spread both inside and outside Cuba concerning the missing Guevara's whereabouts.

There are various rumors from retired Cuban officials who were around the Castro brothers that the Castro brothers and Guevara had a strong disagreement after Guevara's Algiers speech. Intelligence files from the [East German](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") embassy in Cuba detail various heated exchanges between Fidel Castro and Che Guevara after Guevara's return from Africa. Whether Castro disagreed with Guevara's criticisms of the Soviet Union or just found them unproductive to express on the world stage remains unclear.<sup id="cite_ref-215"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>

On 3 October 1965, Castro publicly revealed an undated letter purportedly written to him by Guevara around seven months earlier which was later titled Che Guevara's "farewell letter". In the letter, Guevara reaffirmed his enduring solidarity with the Cuban Revolution but declared his intention to leave Cuba to fight for the revolutionary cause abroad. Additionally, he resigned from all his positions in the Cuban government and communist party, and renounced his honorary Cuban citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-216"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup>

## Congo Crisis

### Military involvement

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CheInCongo1965.jpg)

37-year-old Guevara, holding a Congolese baby and standing with a fellow [Afro-Cuban](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afro-Cubans "Afro-Cubans") soldier in the [Congo Crisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congo_Crisis "Congo Crisis"), 1965

> I tried to make them understand that the real issue was not the liberation of any given state, but a common war against the common master, who was one and the same in Mozambique and in Malawi, in Rhodesia and in South Africa, in the Congo and in Angola, but not one of them agreed.

—Che Guevara, in February 1965, after meeting with various African liberation movement leaders in Dar es Salaam, Tanzania<sup id="cite_ref-217"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup>

In early 1965, Guevara went to Africa to offer his knowledge and experience as a guerrilla to the ongoing [conflict in the Congo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congo_Crisis "Congo Crisis"). According to Algerian President [Ahmed Ben Bella](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_Ben_Bella "Ahmed Ben Bella"), Guevara thought that Africa was imperialism's weak link and so had enormous revolutionary potential.<sup id="cite_ref-218"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> Egyptian President [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser"), who had fraternal relations with Che since his 1959 visit, saw Guevara's plan to fight in Congo as "unwise" and warned that he would become a "[Tarzan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarzan "Tarzan")" figure, doomed to failure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997624_219-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997624-219">[219]</a></sup> Despite the warning, Guevara traveled to Congo using the alias Ramón Benítez.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997629_220-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997629-220">[220]</a></sup> He led the Cuban operation in support of the leftist [Simba movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simba_rebellion "Simba rebellion"), which had emerged from the ongoing Congo conflict. Guevara, his second-in-command [Víctor Dreke](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Dreke "Víctor Dreke"), and 12 other Cuban expeditionaries arrived in Congo on 24 April 1965, and a contingent of approximately 100 [Afro-Cubans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afro-Cubans "Afro-Cubans") joined them soon afterward.<sup id="cite_ref-221"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> For a time, they collaborated with guerrilla leader [Laurent-Désiré Kabila](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila "Laurent-Désiré Kabila"), who had helped supporters of the overthrown prime minister [Patrice Lumumba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba "Patrice Lumumba") to lead an unsuccessful revolt months earlier. As an admirer of the late Lumumba, Guevara declared that his "murder should be a lesson for all of us".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198986_223-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198986-223">[223]</a></sup> Guevara, with limited knowledge of [Swahili](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swahili_language "Swahili language") and the local languages, was assigned a teenage interpreter, Freddy Ilanga. Over the course of seven months, Ilanga grew to "admire the hard-working Guevara", who "showed the same respect to black people as he did to whites".<sup id="cite_ref-224"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Guevara soon became disillusioned with the poor discipline of Kabila's troops and later dismissed him, stating "nothing leads me to believe he is the man of the hour".<sup id="cite_ref-225"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Regardless, Che still regarded Kabila more favorably than other Simba leaders, several of whom still pretended to lead rebel forces even after they had fled into exile.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017158,_160_226-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017158,_160-226">[226]</a></sup>

As an additional obstacle, the Congolese military (the _[Armée Nationale Congolaise](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arm%C3%A9e_Nationale_Congolaise "Armée Nationale Congolaise")_, ANC) was aided by [mercenary troops](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercenaries_and_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo "Mercenaries and the Democratic Republic of the Congo") led by [Mike Hoare](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mad_Mike_Hoare "Mad Mike Hoare") and supported by [anti-Castro Cuban pilots and the CIA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA_activities_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo "CIA activities in the Democratic Republic of the Congo"). These forces thwarted Guevara's movements from his base camp in the mountains near the village of [Fizi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fizi "Fizi") on [Lake Tanganyika](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika "Lake Tanganyika") in southeast Congo. They were able to monitor his communications and so pre-empted his attacks and interdicted his supply lines. Although Guevara tried to conceal his presence in Congo, the United States government knew his location and activities. The [National Security Agency](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Security_Agency "National Security Agency") was intercepting all of his incoming and outgoing transmissions via equipment aboard the [USNS _Private Jose F. Valdez_](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/USNS_Private_Jose_F._Valdez_(T-AG-169) "USNS Private Jose F. Valdez (T-AG-169)"), a floating listening post that continuously cruised the Indian Ocean off [Dar es Salaam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam "Dar es Salaam") for that purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-227"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> After becoming aware of the Communist Cubans' presence in eastern Congo, Hoare planned his strategies to explicitly counter their guerrilla warfare tactics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017153,_161_228-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017153,_161-228">[228]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cheguevaracongo.jpg)

Listening to a [Zenith](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zenith_Electronics "Zenith Electronics") [Trans-Oceanic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-Oceanic "Trans-Oceanic") [shortwave radio receiver](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shortwave_radio_receiver "Shortwave radio receiver") are (seated from the left) Rogelio Oliva, José María Martínez Tamayo (known as "Mbili" in the Congo and "Ricardo" in Bolivia), and Guevara. Standing behind them is Roberto Sánchez ("Lawton" in Cuba and "Changa" in the Congo), 1965.

Guevara's aim was to [export the revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exporting_the_revolution "Exporting the revolution") by instructing local anti-[Mobutu](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko "Mobutu Sese Seko") Simba fighters in Marxist ideology and [foco theory](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foco "Foco") strategies of [guerrilla warfare](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare "Guerrilla warfare"). In his _Congo Diary_ book, he cites a combination of incompetence, intransigence, and infighting among the Congolese rebels as key reasons for the revolt's failure.<sup id="cite_ref-229"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> From September 1965, the ANC and its allies launched [Operation South](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_South "Operation South") to destroy Kabila's forces. With the support of Che and his Cubans, the Simbas put up substantial resistance. Regardless, the rebels were increasingly pushed back, lost their supply routes, and suffered under failing morale.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017153–166_230-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017153%E2%80%93166-230">[230]</a></sup> Guevara himself was almost killed in one clash of the operation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017164_231-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017164-231">[231]</a></sup> Regardless, he initially wanted to continue some form of guerrilla campaign from the local mountains, but even his Simba allies ultimately told him that the rebellion was defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017166–167_232-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVillafana2017166%E2%80%93167-232">[232]</a></sup> On 20 November 1965, suffering from [dysentery](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dysentery "Dysentery") and acute asthma, and disheartened after seven months of defeats and inactivity, Guevara left Congo with the six Cuban survivors of his 12-man column. Guevara stated that he had planned to send the wounded back to Cuba and fight in the Congo alone until his death, as a revolutionary example. But after being urged by his comrades, and two Cuban emissaries personally sent by Castro, at the last moment he reluctantly agreed to leave Africa. During that day and night, Guevara's forces quietly took down their base camp, burned their huts, and destroyed or threw weapons into Lake Tanganyika that they could not take with them, before crossing the border by boat into Tanzania at night and traveling by land to Dar es Salaam. In speaking about his experience in Congo months later, Guevara concluded that he left rather than fight to the death because: "The human element failed. There is no will to fight. The \[rebel\] leaders are corrupt. In a word ... there was nothing to do."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198987_233-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198987-233">[233]</a></sup> Guevara also declared that "we can not liberate, all by ourselves, a country that does not want to fight."<sup id="cite_ref-234"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> A few weeks later, he wrote the preface to the diary he kept during the Congo venture, that began: "This is the story of a failure."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuevara20001_235-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuevara20001-235">[235]</a></sup>

### Flight from the Congo

Following the failure of the rebellion in the Congo, Guevara was reluctant to return to Cuba, because Castro had already made public Guevara's "farewell letter"—a letter intended to only be revealed in the case of his death—wherein he severed all ties in order to devote himself to revolution throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-236"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> As a result, Guevara spent the next six months living clandestinely at the Cuban embassy in Dar es Salaam and later at a Cuban safehouse in [Ládví](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamenice_(Prague-East_District) "Kamenice (Prague-East District)") near Prague.<sup id="cite_ref-237"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> While in Europe, Guevara made a secret visit to former Argentine president [Juan Perón](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Per%C3%B3n "Juan Perón") who lived in exile in [Francoist Spain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francoist_Spain "Francoist Spain") where he confided in Perón about his new plan to formulate a communist revolution to bring all of Latin America under socialist control. Perón warned Guevara that his plans for implementing a communist revolution throughout Latin America, starting with Bolivia, would be suicidal and futile, but Guevara's mind was already made up. Later, Perón remarked that Guevara was "an immature utopian... but one of us. I am happy for it to be so because he is giving the Yankees a real headache."<sup id="cite_ref-ODonnell_238-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-ODonnell-238">[238]</a></sup>

During this time abroad, Guevara compiled his memoirs of the Congo experience and wrote drafts of two more books, one on philosophy and the other on economics. As Guevara prepared for Bolivia, he secretly traveled back to Cuba on 21 July 1966 to visit Castro, as well as to see his wife and to write a last letter to his five children to be read upon his death, which ended with him instructing them:

> Above all, always be capable of feeling deeply any injustice committed against anyone, anywhere in the world. This is the most beautiful quality in a revolutionary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuevara2009167_239-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuevara2009167-239">[239]</a></sup>

## Bolivian insurgency

### Departure to Bolivia

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ernesto_Guevara-Passport1966.png)

Guevara's 1966 passport featuring him in disguise with a false name.

In late 1966, Guevara's location was still not public knowledge, although representatives of Mozambique's independence movement, the [FRELIMO](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/FRELIMO "FRELIMO"), reported that they met with Guevara in [Dar es Salaam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam "Dar es Salaam") regarding his offer to aid in their revolutionary project, an offer which they ultimately rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-240"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> In a speech at the 1967 [International Workers' Day](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Workers%27_Day "International Workers' Day") rally in Havana, the acting minister of the armed forces, Major [Juan Almeida Bosque](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Almeida_Bosque "Juan Almeida Bosque"), announced that Guevara was "serving the revolution somewhere in Latin America".<sup id="cite_ref-241"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> In his book _Opération Condor_ published in 2020, French journalist [Pablo Daniel Magee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pablo_Daniel_Magee "Pablo Daniel Magee") reconstitutes the first incursion of Che Guevara in [Bolivia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolivia "Bolivia") on 3 October 1966, based on top-secret documents kept in the [UNESCO](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") protected [Archives of Terror](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archives_of_Terror "Archives of Terror"), in [Paraguay](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paraguay "Paraguay").

Before he departed for Bolivia, Guevara altered his appearance by shaving off his beard and much of his hair, also dying it grey so that he was unrecognizable as Che Guevara.<sup id="cite_ref-242"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> On 3 November 1966, Guevara secretly arrived in [La Paz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Paz "La Paz") on a flight from Montevideo, under the false name Adolfo Mena González, posing as a middle-aged Uruguayan businessman working for the [Organization of American States](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_of_American_States "Organization of American States").<sup id="cite_ref-243"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup>

Three days after his arrival in Bolivia, Guevara left La Paz for the rural south east region of the country to form his guerrilla army. Guevara's first base camp was located in the [montane dry forest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_dry_broadleaf_forests "Tropical and subtropical dry broadleaf forests") in the remote Ñancahuazú region. Training at the camp in the Ñancahuazú valley proved to be hazardous, and little was accomplished in way of building a guerrilla army. The Argentine-born [East German](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") operative [Tamara Bunke](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamara_Bunke "Tamara Bunke"), better known by her _[nom de guerre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudonym#Military_and_paramilitary_organizations "Pseudonym")_ "Tania", had been installed as Che's primary agent in La Paz.<sup id="cite_ref-#refSelvage1985|Selvage_1985_244-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-#refSelvage1985%7CSelvage_1985-244">[244]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997693_245-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1997693-245">[245]</a></sup>

### Ñancahuazú Guerrilla

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CheinBolivia1.jpg)

Guevara in rural Bolivia, shortly before his death (1967)

Guevara's guerrilla force, numbering about 50 men<sup id="cite_ref-246"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> and operating as the ELN (_Ejército de Liberación Nacional de Bolivia_, "National Liberation Army of Bolivia"), was well equipped and scored a number of early successes against Bolivian army regulars [in the difficult terrain of the mountainous Camiri region during the early months of 1967](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_of_Che "Route of Che"). As a result of Guevara's units winning several skirmishes against Bolivian troops in the spring and summer of 1967, the Bolivian government began to overestimate the true size of the guerrilla force.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellner198997_247-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellner198997-247">[247]</a></sup>

Researchers hypothesize that Guevara's plan for fomenting a revolution in Bolivia failed for an array of reasons:

-   Guevara had expected assistance and cooperation from the local dissidents that he did not receive, nor did he receive support from Bolivia's Communist Party under the leadership of [Mario Monje](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mario_Monje "Mario Monje"), which was oriented toward Moscow rather than Havana. In Guevara's own diary captured after his death, he wrote about the [Communist Party of Bolivia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Bolivia "Communist Party of Bolivia"), which he characterized as "distrustful, disloyal and stupid".<sup id="cite_ref-248"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup>
-   He had expected to deal only with the Bolivian military, who were poorly trained and equipped, and was unaware that the United States government had sent a team of the [CIA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency "Central Intelligence Agency")'s [Special Activities Division](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Activities_Center "Special Activities Center") commandos and other operatives into Bolivia to aid the anti-insurrection effort. The [Bolivian Army](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolivian_Army "Bolivian Army") was also trained, advised, and supplied by [US Army Special Forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army_Special_Forces "United States Army Special Forces"), including an elite battalion of [US Rangers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army_Rangers "United States Army Rangers") trained in [jungle warfare](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jungle_warfare "Jungle warfare") that set up camp in La Esperanza, a small settlement close to the location of Guevara's guerrillas.<sup id="cite_ref-249"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup>
-   He had expected to remain in radio contact with Havana. The two [shortwave radio](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shortwave_radio "Shortwave radio") transmitters provided to him by Cuba were faulty.
